  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText8173047080801649690" style="display:none">"Y" is none other than unemployed escape artist Yorick Brown (his father was a Shakespeare buff), and he's seemingly the only male human left alive after a mysterious plague kills all Y-chromosome carriers on earth. But why are he and his faithful companion, the often testy male monkey Ampersand, still alive? He sets out to find the answer (and his girlfriend), while running from angry female Republicans (now running the government), Amazon wannabes that include his own sister (seemingly brainwashed), and other threats. The Vertigo team of Brian K. Vaughan, Pia Guerra, and José Marzán Jr. have given us a great read!<br /><br />Collects Y: The Last Man issues #01-#05</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_564288').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_564288').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_564288').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_132769949" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132769949" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1036930-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583425448p2/1036930.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132769949?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/1036930-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1036930-michael?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1036930-michael?shelf=1990s">1990s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1036930-michael?shelf=most-popular-reviews">most-popular-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132769949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer589970359312811333">In typical comic book male-centric fashion, this series wonders what life would be like if all men died spontaneously...except for one. <br/><br/>I suppose if we're trying to put ourselves in the head of an early-nineties comic book reading teen, this might feel innovative. Unfortunately, I find that innovative in the world of comics is pretty much Iron Age for the rest of literature. How does Vaughan manage to make a series with gender issues at its center so bizarrely sexist? <br/><br/>Example: In a world where a</span>
  <span id="freeText589970359312811333" style="display:none">In typical comic book male-centric fashion, this series wonders what life would be like if all men died spontaneously...except for one. <br><br>I suppose if we're trying to put ourselves in the head of an early-nineties comic book reading teen, this might feel innovative. Unfortunately, I find that innovative in the world of comics is pretty much Iron Age for the rest of literature. How does Vaughan manage to make a series with gender issues at its center so bizarrely sexist? <br><br>Example: In a world where all men are dead except for one, and the death of that one man will mean the end of humanity, VIOLENT CULTS OF FEMINISTS SPRING UP TO TRY AND HUNT DOWN MEN AND MALE SYMPATHIZERS. What is the motive here? There sure isn't one written into the plot, other than the one speech about social inequality between the sexes--and how the only way to escape this inequality is to KILL ALL MEN. <br><br>Characterwise, I was exceptionally not impressed. Even the main character has vague motivations. As for the women, pretty much none of them function as anything but placeholders: the token love interest, the sister who has gone astray, the protective mother. IN A WORLD WHERE ONLY ONE MAN SURVIVED...apparently the world still revolves around that man. <br><br>And here's where the cultural rant starts...<br><br>This is a symptom of thinking that is still prevalent in most of popular culture, although not to as great an extent in literature. F'rinstance, lets talk about movies: movies are a great medium for making political statements. Statements about social injustices, such as the way that women are objectified, sexualized, expected to live up to some bleached, shaved, makeup-smeared, surgically modified yet waifishly thin ideal that has been developed over centuries of patriarchal society...and how this objectification upon women is psychologically damaging--to men.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380341928i/697888.jpg" width="250" height="223" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This poor guy above has been so mentally warped by Hollywood and advertising that he's incapable of developing a physical attraction to any of the normal girls he knows in real life. Let's take a moment to pitty him. <br><br><br><br>Okay, we done? Good. Fortunately, a blonde porn star moves in next door, and immediately falls for him, even though he's intensely dorky, because, you know, it's what's on the inside that counts. But, I'm not just cherry-picking films here. I could point to this one:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380341928i/697889._SX540_.jpg" width="280" height="190" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Another example of an attractive woman with a *cough cough* career who ends up with a loser whose only redeeming trait is that he's willing to "raise" the baby...if sleazy frat boys without jobs can be said to raise babies. <br><br>But surely this is a phenomenon in teen comedies?<br><br>Well, look at "romances."<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380341928i/697890.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Here's a fairly recent romantic comedy where a successful, relatively well-balanced woman who is portrayed as HORRIBLY DESPARATE for being interested in a neighbor....meanwhile, the character played by Gerard Butler mudwrestles with models on television, and has no interest in anything but one-night stands, yet this is understandable because of his childhood. This is a ROMANCE. Aren't these supposed to be geared more towards female audiences? It really bothers me that I'm more bothered by this film than any women I know. <br><br>End rant. <br><br>Okay, BUT, regardless of how inadequately this comic deals with gender issues, it at least TRIES to grapple with them, and it does a better job than any of the movies mentioned above. Perhaps by the end of the series, the author's portrayals of gender issues will become more interesting and sophisticated. This was an entertaining comic, and I plan on continuing it for at least a little longer...but I'll admit that I'm highly confused by the acclaim it has gotten. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="589970359312811333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_250011869" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/250011869" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/250011869?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">The Fool on the Hill</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=shite">shite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=hopes-dashed-like-an-egg-on-cement">hopes-dashed-like-an-egg-on-cement</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=comic-books">comic-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=curiousity-killed-the-bananas">curiousity-killed-the-bananas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=apocalypse">apocalypse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer250011869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer929255843546346005">So there's this thing that happens in post-apocalypse stories that I need to talk to you about. <br/><br/>You know how in a zombiepocalypse story we occassionally receive hints that it might be better for the women to stay safe so they can make babies? Usually it's only hints, and the male characters don't seem to want to offend the post-feminist sensibilities of the women, so instead the women tote guns and put their wombs at risk of becoming a zombie-buffet. But everyone gets along-ish, and there are us</span>
  <span id="freeText929255843546346005" style="display:none">So there's this thing that happens in post-apocalypse stories that I need to talk to you about. <br /><br />You know how in a zombiepocalypse story we occassionally receive hints that it might be better for the women to stay safe so they can make babies? Usually it's only hints, and the male characters don't seem to want to offend the post-feminist sensibilities of the women, so instead the women tote guns and put their wombs at risk of becoming a zombie-buffet. But everyone gets along-ish, and there are usually plenty of women and men, so it doesn't seem like fertility is the <i>most</i> important concern. <br /><br />Or you get the big, bad group of fascist men trying to turn some poor girl into a "breeder" for the new human race, but she tends to rise up, spank their patriarchal asses, escape with her girl power intact, and hook up with some nice guy with whom she's fought for survival. <br /><br />And in the bleakest of apocalypses there's no hope anyway, so who gives a shit about procreation? Everyone's dead or dying, cannibalism is running rampant, society has failed, and humans are doomed to extinction. The best the survivors can do is keep hiking down some road to whatever is further down the road with the world as nothing but the road.<br /><br />But I've totally fucking had it now that I've read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/156534.Y_The_Last_Man__Vol__1_Unmanned" title="Y The Last Man, Vol. 1 Unmanned by Brian K. Vaughan" rel="nofollow noopener">Y: The Last Man</a>. This book really pisses me off to no end.<br /><br />I'm fine with the Amazonian self-mutilators (I can buy an angry, post-apocalyptic group of violent women). I am willing to suspend my disbelief that Yorick and his monkey make it through the manpocalypse as the only surviving Y chromosomes. I'll yawn and tolerate the Yankee setting of yet another apocalypse. I'll cringe but cope with yet another bad ass, dreadlocked, African-American woman who's the most capable and violent person around. I'll even believe that spindly little Yorick can pass as a woman as long as he has his gas mask on. <br /><br />But what I won't believe, what I won't buy, where I won't suspend by disbelief, where I am not fine is with the idea that Yorick would ever, EVER, be allowed to wander around the winter of homo sapienism with one body guard, risking his testicles for some stupid, pointless, selfish, idiotic search for the love of his life and his sister. His sperm, and Ampersand's, would be the most important substances known to womankind (not because he is a man but because of sheer practicality). He would be protected whether he liked it or not. He would be imprisoned. His sperm would be used to impregnate. It would be used to find an immunity for future boys. It would be used for the survival of homo sapiens. Period. <br /><br />I heard this book was really great -- a must read graphic novel. At best it is okay ... if you look past the idiocy of Yorick's wanderings, his insufferable smarminess, that stupid fucking monkey, and the poorest characterizations of women you're ever likely to see. Why two stars then? Because it isn't quite as bad as the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/151715.Joshua_Luna" title="Joshua Luna" rel="nofollow noopener">Luna Brothers</a>' <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/316446.Girls_Volume_1_Conception__Girls_" title="Girls Volume 1 Conception (Girls) by Joshua Luna" rel="nofollow noopener">Girls</a> -- though it is damn close.</span>
  <a data-text-id="929255843546346005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2079420999" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2079420999" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2079420999?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2079420999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13818608008174152164">This book is such a neat concept, but there's 4 things I'm stuck on.<br/><br/>1. it's a book about a world run by women after all the men die, yet it's still told from the POV of a man because conveniently !!!! one survives. I think I would have loved this more if we were given a story of a world with just all women, because heaven knows we could survive without that one man. <br/><br/>2. This book was way, way, way, way more political than I was expecting it to be. The mother of the MC works in Washington so a lot</span>
  <span id="freeText13818608008174152164" style="display:none">This book is such a neat concept, but there's 4 things I'm stuck on.<br /><br />1. it's a book about a world run by women after all the men die, yet it's still told from the POV of a man because conveniently !!!! one survives. I think I would have loved this more if we were given a story of a world with just all women, because heaven knows we could survive without that one man. <br /><br />2. This book was way, way, way, way more political than I was expecting it to be. The mother of the MC works in Washington so a lot of this concerned the government and what to do once a bunch of the male politicians died, and that was cool for a few pages, but got old really fast? I'm sure this will get more interesting throughout the next books, but it was a bit repetitive. <br /><br />3. I feel like this just feeds the negative image and stereotype of radical feminists. One main antagonist in this book is a group of women called the Amazons who burn sperm banks and basically celebrate the end of men, which I think is farfetched and a bit inappropriate. Even if some women did this, I don't think they would play as major of a role as they did in this book, and I think this misleading depiction could rub off wrong on readers and make feminism seem more militant than it actually is. <br /><br />4. One of the first things I thought of when I started this was the topic of trans men and how they would be treated and/or react to this situation. I think it would have been awesome to spotlight a trans man navigating this new world. However, this book handled it so poorly. The one mention of a trans man is to tell the reader that he was murdered by the Amazons because they didn't think any men should continue to live. Additionally, a slur (tr*nny) was used to address this person, AND he was misgendered and called a "she" whenever his death was described. <br /><br />This book was written/set in 2002, so I anticipate some of those flaws and the political incorrectness may derive from its outdatedness, but I still couldn't get over those few things.<br /><br />But other than that, I had a great time reading it. The art is nice. It's funny. It's easy to follow, and one of the only graphic novels i've read in a while that I'm eager to find the sequels to immediately.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13818608008174152164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122744671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15366551099245698825">I haven’t read a comic book since I was a child, saving my measly allowance for Archie and his friends. Once I discovered my mother’s Harold Robbins novels, I never went back to comics…until now.<br/><br/>A number of my Goodreads friends enjoy graphic novels (as they are called now), so I became curious and asked my friend <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/405390-kemper' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kemper</a> for a recommendation. Y: The Last Man was perfect for me to start with. I love post-apocalyptic stories and wanted some light, easy reading between school books.<br/><br/>A plague that des</span>
  <span id="freeText15366551099245698825" style="display:none">I haven’t read a comic book since I was a child, saving my measly allowance for Archie and his friends. Once I discovered my mother’s Harold Robbins novels, I never went back to comics…until now.<br /><br />A number of my Goodreads friends enjoy graphic novels (as they are called now), so I became curious and asked my friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/405390-kemper" rel="nofollow noopener">Kemper</a> for a recommendation. Y: The Last Man was perfect for me to start with. I love post-apocalyptic stories and wanted some light, easy reading between school books.<br /><br />A plague that destroys the world’s male population, except a young man and his monkey. Amazons who want to rid the world of the last vestige of male oppression. A model who disposes of corpses. A mysterious agent who knits. Republicans with guns. Humorous dialogue, great illustrations, fun characters and a fast-paced story made me gobble this up in one sitting. <br /><br />Looking forward to more!<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15880858441296056360">The story started out so well: fast-paced, intriguing..I can see it's a dude comic, the main character ends up being the last man left on a planet full of allll kinds of women!   <span id="freeText15880858441296056360" style="display:none">The story started out so well: fast-paced, intriguing..I can see it's a dude comic, the main character ends up being the last man left on a planet full of allll kinds of women! No matter what kind of an ugly twat you might wanna be, <i>some</i> woman will want you. <b>Yessss!</b><br>I see half-naked blonde, beachy-style woman, some ex-models running around, army women, special op women, scientist women. That's ookayyy with me. It <i>is</i> a dude comic, after all, no?<br><br>Then came this:<br><b>Yorick</b> (main char): I'm not afraid of the world...I'm fraid of a world without you. I mean it, Beth. I really feel lost when we're apart. <br><b>Beth</b>: I know. I've missed you too, Yorick. I was just thinking about the time we were on the roof in the rain...<br><b>Yorick</b>: But it's not just that! I mean, of course I miss that, but...You're my best friend, Beth. You're brilliant and funny and your favorite movie is Miller's Crossing. I didn't even know there were women like you.<br><br>Later the main char (hereafter referred to as: Twat) says to his mother:<br><b>Twat</b>: But I don't want to sit here and be a...a "stud" for however many anonymous women you expect me to inseminate. Not when the girl I <b>love</b> is out there. (He blankly stares through the window)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380386324ra/745760.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>No, man! NO! Don't do this to me!<br><br>So much for the dude-comic. Ok.<br><br><br>So, next we see Twat encounter a woman that seems to be picking up dead bodies and driving them in a garbage truck in order to exchange them for canned food. I won't even go there, but what I wish to point out is the following: remember Jill from Resident Evil 3? I was always pissed that she's fighting infectious zombies half-naked, when her priority is to shield herself from their bites at any cost? I'd armor up! Now, this tschik seems to do the same. She's an ex-super model, trying to lift the male dead bodies (of 80-100kg each) and toss 'em into the garbage truck. There is <b>no</b> way she can do this alone without getting in heavy body contact with half- or nearly rotten dead bodies. Did I mention that it is also nighttime?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380386324i/745761._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380386324i/745762._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Moving on! What appears next seems to be the development of Twat's character, where we see that he's not only a gentle lover, but also momma's boy:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380386324i/745763._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And anyway, what could POSSIBLY be worst than the dreadful terrorists that seem to be aiming straight (and only) at America?!<br><br>[pause for more drama]<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380386324i/745764._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380386324ra/745765.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay. Leave that be [I won't even go into the topic where the women in power state how the dead men's Constitution doesn't apply anymore, because it is <i>their</i> constitution and that it's time for something NEW! Fuckyea!].<br><br>So, we come to the main problem. It's manpocalypse and the President decides that the <b>last left man on earth</b> (being as they're apparently too late to grab hold of the sperm bank/s) is being sent on a journey with a: "Godspeed to you both and whatever you do...don't fuck this up"<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>Now, I don't know about you, but I'd shackle dat man and milk him! Something like..well, this:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380386324i/745767.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>[One thing I <i>don't</i> get to complain about is the artwork :) love it!]<br><br>I definitely wouldn't let the immature twat set off on a journey guarded by only one person, no matter how spec op they may be. *shakes head* <br><br>Oh, and while we're at the White House scene, lookie at this *tries to suppress her chuckle. No, not really :'D gahahahaha*<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380386324i/745768.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380386324ra/745769.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>If <i>they</i> did it, you better watch out for what the <i>others</i> do, some srs sh*t!<br><br>We also have the Amazons who go all Altair on their breast so they can handle the bow better. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380386324i/745770.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In the world of powerful firearms and effective cold weapons you chose a..bow? Bow-chicks become popular in 2012, <i>not</i> in the time of the Last Man so nu-huuhhh! <br><br>Don't even get me started on Dr. Allison, where the throws herself at developing a breast cancer cure for the last generation livin' on this planet:<br><b>Dr.</b>"If we're going to be the last generation of humans, we should at least be allowed to live our miserable lives in good health."<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380386324ra/745771.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*sigh* :'D <br><br>Why am I so angry at this comic and I've just started?<br>It's 'cause the main character pisses me SO off! He's got great responsibility now and he he literally waits for the moment when his guard looks away for him to go make some shi*. Not only he's totally consumed with seeing his darling did-she-agree-to-marry-him-or-not? fiance [<b>Twat</b>: We both know that I resent you dragging me to some attack-of-the-clones doctor when I could be out there looking for the girl I love. FINE.], he's all too immature [<b>Twat</b>: Jesus, where the hell do you get off lecturing me like I'm some kind of delinquent kid? We're practically the same age! <b>355 aka Guard</b>: then start acting like it, Yorick!&gt; AND he's a grammar Nazi!<br>*sigh* he doesn't deserve the harem he's got himself into...<br><br>I forgot what were the positive things I was gonna point out and the reason it actually got two stars instead of one but..<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380386324ra/745772.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nevermind.</span>

<div id="review_258431122" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258431122" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6773727-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579036502p2/6773727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/258431122?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/6773727-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6773727-shannon?shelf=need-reviewing">need-reviewing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6773727-shannon?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer258431122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16935758953296518107">What if all the men, except one young man and his male monkey pet, were wiped out all over the world and nobody knew why exactly? That's the setup for volume one of this series that takes a look at gender issues and progressive science versus a natural order of things. I like that the explanation for the plague is not known and there are several possibilities. <br/><br/>There's a fair amount of mischievous style humor in the first volume. For instance, women commemorate the dead man at an obvious phallic </span>
  <span id="freeText16935758953296518107" style="display:none">What if all the men, except one young man and his male monkey pet, were wiped out all over the world and nobody knew why exactly? That's the setup for volume one of this series that takes a look at gender issues and progressive science versus a natural order of things. I like that the explanation for the plague is not known and there are several possibilities. <br /><br />There's a fair amount of mischievous style humor in the first volume. For instance, women commemorate the dead man at an obvious phallic symbol a la The Washington Monument. Extremists women take on the role of the ancient Amazons and tear off one breast and take to believing Mother Earth meant to eradicate the males. Hardcore GOPs may take offense when Republican wives of dead senators show up with guns, arguing they should have a voice in the new government. <br /><br />The main character, Yorick, is a putz and sometimes clueless but believable enough even though some might argue he is a passive character. The super model turned corpse collector who just got her implants is an obvious jab at how the fashion industry and of course female looks are intertwined with male desires. Overall, I'd say this is a very good start but if you're the nitpicking type you may not enjoy it as much because everything hasn't been explained. <br /><br />A good starting read, by the way, for people new to comics/graphic novels. <br /><br />The series has received 5 prestigious Eisner Awards. Hollywood has been trying to make this into a movie since 2007. Some say this series saved Vertigo Comics from financial problems. <br /><br /><b>CHARACTERS/DIALOGUE: B plus; STORY/PLOTTING: B plus to A minus; ARTWORK: B plus; THEMES: B to B plus; WHEN READ: early January 2012; OVERALL GRADE: B plus. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16935758953296518107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1795442083" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1795442083" />
    <a title="Brian Yahn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22849115-brian-yahn"><img alt="Brian Yahn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464719293p2/22849115.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1795442083?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian Yahn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian Yahn" href="/user/show/22849115-brian-yahn">Brian Yahn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1795442083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10175615612858769702"><i>Y: The Last Man</i> has a great premise -- all males (of every species) suddenly die -- except one. The story focuses on the lone male survivor and is an unraveling of why / how he survived the mysterious scourge.<br/><br/>It helps that the last man standing is humorous and likable like so many of Brian K. Vaughan's characters. Also that he has this noble desire to make it to the other side of the world to reunite with his girlfriend (and repopulate the world). The story is essentially about all the things ge</span>
  <span id="freeText10175615612858769702" style="display:none"><i>Y: The Last Man</i> has a great premise -- all males (of every species) suddenly die -- except one. The story focuses on the lone male survivor and is an unraveling of why / how he survived the mysterious scourge.<br /><br />It helps that the last man standing is humorous and likable like so many of Brian K. Vaughan's characters. Also that he has this noble desire to make it to the other side of the world to reunite with his girlfriend (and repopulate the world). The story is essentially about all the things getting in his way.<br /><br />I wish this installment had a little more of a closing to it, but either way, I still want to read more.</span>

  <span id="freeText1759768745079726831" style="display:none"><b>If you are a woman,<br />You might have to sleep with me<br />Since I'm the Last Man on Earth<br />And there ain't nothing wrong with me</b><br /><i>Loudon Wainwright III</i><br /><br /><br />Meet Yorick, an unemployed English major with moderate-to-poor computer skills. And, oh yeah, his hobby is magic.<br /><br />You probably wouldn't sleep with him if he was the...well, nevermind.<br /><br />There he is, ladies - The Last Man on Earth.<br /><br />The dating pool has just gotten a little smaller thanks to a mysterious plague that has wiped out all males, cute puppies and kittens included, on the planet. All except for the above mentioned guy and the male helper monkey he's fostering. <br /><br />Yeah. It takes a little getting used to...<br /><br />So what are the gals up to? Surprisingly, they're not laying in a supply of batteries, or rejoicing in that toilet seat thing being forever solved...like I would be. No. Everyone seems to have an agenda, and there are a lot of kick-ass broads out there. So much for Peace on Earth with the women in charge. There are power struggles aplenty.<br /><br />This volume does a great job of setting up the series. I liked the old-fashioned comic book look of it, and the attention to detail. <br /><br />Alas, as poor Yorick and his bodyguard, Agent 355 (she really needs a nickname), set out to find the cause of the plague and a possible cure, we're left with many questions that HAD BETTER be answered in the next volumes, not the least of which is, will Yorick be able to remain faithful to his sweetie when he kind of needs to repopulate the human race?<br /><br />I know a good man is hard to find, but this is ridiculous. </span>

<div id="review_437920689" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/437920689" />
    <a title="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party"><img alt="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562621595p2/10923016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/437920689?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" href="/user/show/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party">David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=favorite-books-or-series">favorite-books-or-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=graphic-novels-are-cool">graphic-novels-are-cool</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=vertigo">vertigo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=five-inges-because-inge-is-a-star">five-inges-because-inge-is-a-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer437920689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5786010358713799468">Ask a comic-book geek what the greatest graphic novel of all time was, and at least 9 out of 10 will tell you it's "Watchmen". And there's no denying Watchmen deserves the accolades it gets, as it quite effectively reinvented the graphic novel genre. However, if you asked THIS comic-book geek what the greatest graphic novel of all time was, and I would instantly tell you it's "Y The Last Man"!<br/><br/>The book starts out with an intriguing premise...a mysterious plague instantly kills off every man on th</span>
  <span id="freeText5786010358713799468" style="display:none">Ask a comic-book geek what the greatest graphic novel of all time was, and at least 9 out of 10 will tell you it's "Watchmen". And there's no denying Watchmen deserves the accolades it gets, as it quite effectively reinvented the graphic novel genre. However, if you asked THIS comic-book geek what the greatest graphic novel of all time was, and I would instantly tell you it's "Y The Last Man"!<br /><br />The book starts out with an intriguing premise...a mysterious plague instantly kills off every man on the planet...except for one young man named Yorick Brown. Now, as all the women around the world start to rebuild a society without any men, Yorick goes on a quest to try to learn exactly why he survived the plague. A tale of such epic proportions would have been too much for many writers, but Brian K. Vaughan not only takes the story to its fullest potential, he manages to somehow exceed even that! And the rich, detailed artwork by Pia Guerra is exactly the icing this cake needs. <br /><br />There are so many layers to this story, it's impossible to really touch on everything in one review. Yorick is a fascinating and likeable protagonist. and his quest to learn the truth about himself and the plague is very exciting, but that's really just one out of many elements that makes this such a fun read. Oftentimes, the ladies who were left behind after all the men died are the ones who steal the show. Brian K. Vaughan works in social commentary on many different issues, including sexism, partisan politics, xenophobia, religion and fanaticism. A lesser writer would have come off as preachy, but Vaughan makes everything flow so naturally that you never feel like you're being lectured. Rather than making his point through ham-fisted techniques, Vaughan simply gives you a cerebral, thought-provoking story and trusts that you'll be able to read all the subtext yourself.<br /><br />Another thing that is so amazing about this story is how real it feels. Sure, a plague killing off all the men and none of the women is pretty over-the-top, but the characters themselves are so deep and fleshed-out, they make the story feel completely genuine. As the women cope with losing all the men in their lives, there are a lot of emotions that play out...enough that I had tears in my eyes more than once while reading the series! This is no cheesy popcorn movie that focuses solely on the action, we watch the characters as they fall in love, lose loved ones, become consumed with rage, and struggle to survive. And every bit of emotion that the characters feel is presented so strongly, the reader feels them as well.<br /><br />Anyone who thinks comic books are immature has never read this powerful, Shakespearean story. I highly recommend you read this first volume of one of the greatest stories ever told. No matter what your literary preference is, I guarantee this book has something in it you'll love! </span>
  <a data-text-id="5786010358713799468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_32817436" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/32817436" />
    <a title="Bruce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/897874-bruce"><img alt="Bruce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1202929351p2/897874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/32817436?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bruce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bruce" href="/user/show/897874-bruce">Bruce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">teens, avid comics fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Bruce by: </span>
      Washington Post comics blog commenter
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/897874-bruce?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/897874-bruce?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer32817436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17001880773767942322">I've read so much here and elsewhere about how brilliant this series is, and from the two books I've read, I'm afraid I can't agree. The concept (plague instantaneously kills all Y-chromosome mammals -- except a guy named Yorick and his pet capuchin monkey -- around the globe without warning) has tremendous <i>promise</i>. However, the execution in the two books I read (this one and Vol. 13) was pedestrian. Characterization, plot, and art were all two-dimensional. (By contrast, Judge Parker has more nu</span>
  <span id="freeText17001880773767942322" style="display:none">I've read so much here and elsewhere about how brilliant this series is, and from the two books I've read, I'm afraid I can't agree. The concept (plague instantaneously kills all Y-chromosome mammals -- except a guy named Yorick and his pet capuchin monkey -- around the globe without warning) has tremendous <i>promise</i>. However, the execution in the two books I read (this one and Vol. 13) was pedestrian. Characterization, plot, and art were all two-dimensional. (By contrast, Judge Parker has more nuance in the latter category.)<br /><br />By way of example, here's a bit of dialogue (all characters have the same or similar wise-cracking persona) from pp. 74-75 of this graphic novel [panels cut back and forth among disputants, mostly mid-shot seen from the POV of someone relatively tall]:<br /><br />"Who the hell are <b>you?</b>"<br /><br />"...<b>I'm</b> the President of the United States. And I say drop the goddamn weapons." ...<br /><br />"Secretary Valentine, we... we thought you were <b>dead.</b>"<br /><br />"Don't listen to them, Margaret! The Democrats just shot Bill Woodring's <b>wife!</b>"<br /><br />"After you <b>murdered</b> an innocent secret service agent!"<br /><br />"You don't understand, we... we didn't have a <b>choice.</b> They've seized control of the White House." ...<br /><br />"Madam President, Congress has only been doing exactly what the Founding Fathers <b>intended.</b>"<br /><br />"The Founding Fathers are <b>dead! All</b> of the men are dead! Their Constitution doesn't <b>apply</b> anymore!"<br /><br />[C-U PRESIDENT'S FACE listening:] "It's time for something <b>new.</b>"<br /><br />In this universe, the ladies appear inclined to shoot first and ask questions later. Anarchy, violence, and hysteria reign. Each scene is a mini-melodrama. This is not an Alan Moore book (contrast "From Hell," which was about Jack the Ripper, and had both less page-to-page violence and substantially more nuance).<br /><br />That said, this first book of the series really exists solely to accomplish 3 tasks: introduce the premise, the principal characters, and establish the quest-like framework for the story (here's this wicked world, now try getting cross-country). The first two are accomplished with the first 34 pages (the initiating comic in this compilation). The last waits on the penultimate page of the graphic novel.<br /><br />There are a few artistic grace notes here, such as the birds-eye view of an urban Y-intersection on the last page after the leads have determined that they will have to hike from Boston to California (no, no city yet named), but for the most part, sophisticated readers seeking other than lightly-buttered popcorn will be disappointed. It should be interesting to see how the film version of this book stacks up against "Children of Men." I'm sure buzz will be high when it gets released, but personally, I'd wait on raves before plunking down my ten bucks.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17001880773767942322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_41068000" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41068000" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1728975-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1230447870p2/1728975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/41068000?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/1728975-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41068000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7563894409938059617">so - while i realize that the premise of this book is supposed to be stunning in overturning the stereotypical assumption that women without men will create a feminist/lesbian utopia, a la Herland, by proposing that left to their own devices, women would act like a bunch of goomba guys, arm themselves and create civil war, strife, and general mayhem, can any of us really image a scenario in which large groups of women, left without men for extended periods of time, would NOT 1) hug a lot 2) lick</span>
  <span id="freeText7563894409938059617" style="display:none">so - while i realize that the premise of this book is supposed to be stunning in overturning the stereotypical assumption that women without men will create a feminist/lesbian utopia, a la Herland, by proposing that left to their own devices, women would act like a bunch of goomba guys, arm themselves and create civil war, strife, and general mayhem, can any of us really image a scenario in which large groups of women, left without men for extended periods of time, would NOT 1) hug a lot 2) lick each others pussies 3) feel weird but talk it out and 4) begin building some sort of egalitarian communal society from the ruins, which, despite its passive-aggressive penal code and lack of vertical monuments, would still probably feed, clothe and manage the resources of the planet less recklessly than anything ever devised by men?</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3139964173?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="HBalikov" class="user" itemprop="url" name="HBalikov" href="/user/show/929238-hbalikov">HBalikov</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3139964173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16134353674701256126">Stephen King says, “The best graphic novel I’ve ever read.” But do we know how many Mr. King has read?<br/><br/>It is certainly a very well-drawn book thanks to Pia Guerra and Jose Marzan, Jr. It has an inventive plot involving the collapse and death of every mammal with a “Y” chromosome with the possible exception of Yorick Brown, escape artist, and his monkey companion, Ampersand. <br/><br/>The story moves at a fast pace, even with its complex plot. The brutality of this brave, new world is sporadically relieved </span>
  <span id="freeText16134353674701256126" style="display:none">Stephen King says, “The best graphic novel I’ve ever read.” But do we know how many Mr. King has read?<br /><br />It is certainly a very well-drawn book thanks to Pia Guerra and Jose Marzan, Jr. It has an inventive plot involving the collapse and death of every mammal with a “Y” chromosome with the possible exception of Yorick Brown, escape artist, and his monkey companion, Ampersand. <br /><br />The story moves at a fast pace, even with its complex plot. The brutality of this brave, new world is sporadically relieved by humor that ranges from black to slapstick. Here is one example: <br />“Aw, I love your monkey! He’s sweet!”<br />“Yeah, well, so‘s the smell of burning flesh. Doesn’t mean it’s good.”<br /><br /> It is clear why King has put his stamp of approval on this. It tracks many of his themes starting with his iconic, The Stand. Don’t misunderstand me – this is a fresh book with a complex plot built from the premise up. We get some of Vaughan’s well-considered speculation on what the USA/world might be like without men. Further, we are led deep into the competing goals of the remaining humans and how many aspects of government, industry, life, etc., might not be functioning as intended. For example, I am looking forward to seeing how Vaughan decides to handle the growing lack of animal protein in the diet since all mammals face the same issue of no males to procreate. No eggs, no milk or other dairy products will be found after a short while. The devil might be in such details.<br /><br />This is book one in a series of five. It’s easy to get on this train; I’m hoping the ride remains this interesting. 4.5*</span>
  <a data-text-id="16134353674701256126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16766157576290321806" style="display:none">This is the first graphic novel I've read, so far. Because after this one..I'm hooked! Yorick is a young guy, wondering where is his place on this planet. He can't find a job, he loves magic and his girlfriend, Beth. She travelled to Australia, to be all smart and to gain some experiences in anthropology, so now Yorick is all alone, feeling like a loser, because he's not doing anything remotely as important as she and the rest of his friends do. <span id="freeTextContainer17570313381603071553">A sort of reversal of the film 'Children of Men', Y the Last Man is sometimes difficult to take seriously. The storytelling itself is not bad, though it sometimes falls into the faults of Lost, with endless, predictable hardship. It is an interesting concept, and Vaughan at least connects himself tangentially to the literary tradition, but these connections are often too flimsy or too coincidental in construction.<br/><br/>The worst crime of all may be that one keeps feeling that Yorick is standing in as </span>
  <span id="freeText17570313381603071553" style="display:none">A sort of reversal of the film 'Children of Men', Y the Last Man is sometimes difficult to take seriously. The storytelling itself is not bad, though it sometimes falls into the faults of Lost, with endless, predictable hardship. It is an interesting concept, and Vaughan at least connects himself tangentially to the literary tradition, but these connections are often too flimsy or too coincidental in construction.<br /><br />The worst crime of all may be that one keeps feeling that Yorick is standing in as an author surrogate; he is the last man on Earth, after all. Of course, anyone writing this story would have to come up against this challenge, but by not really addressing the character's sexual conflict, or his motivations in general, it can begin to feel like an escapist harem romp.<br /><br /><b>
  <a href="http://starsbeetlesandfools.blogspot.com/2013/09/suggested-readings-in-comics.html" rel="nofollow noopener">My Suggested Readings in Comics</a>
</b></span>

<div id="review_838035523" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/838035523" />
    <a title="Selkie ✦ Queen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28165536-selkie-queen"><img alt="Selkie ✦ Queen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587803822p2/28165536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/838035523?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Selkie ✦ Queen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Selkie ✦ Queen" href="/user/show/28165536-selkie-queen">Selkie ✦ Queen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28165536-selkie-queen?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28165536-selkie-queen?shelf=2016-graphic-novel-reads">2016-graphic-novel-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer838035523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4777323175084704343">This comic book series has received rave reviews for its rather satirical premise concerning the idea of the extinction of all mammals with the Y chromosome, and how the female population supposedly tries to deal with this global crisis. I've been intrigued by this series for four years now, but put off reading it even after I bought an actual copy about three years ago. It's a Vertigo title which immediately guarantees it's promising. Finally, I got to read the first volume Unmanned which colle</span>
  <span id="freeText4777323175084704343" style="display:none">This comic book series has received rave reviews for its rather satirical premise concerning the idea of the extinction of all mammals with the Y chromosome, and how the female population supposedly tries to deal with this global crisis. I've been intrigued by this series for four years now, but put off reading it even after I bought an actual copy about three years ago. It's a Vertigo title which immediately guarantees it's promising. Finally, I got to read the first volume Unmanned which collected the first five issues of the series, and as much as I wasn't completely invested yet in the story and characters, I have to agree that it's an interesting beginning.<br><br><i>
  <b>Y: The Last Man</b>
</i> was published in 2002 with ten volume all in all, and its official run ended by 2008. It had received and won nominations from Eisner Awards thrice. That being said, this first volume is not something I would personally consider an instant masterpiece which was okay. Neil Gaiman's <i>The Sandman: Preludes and Nocturnes</i> wasn't so hot either at least until <i>The Sound of Her Wings</i> closing issue, but that series eventually did become one as the story went on. To compare it with the other graphic novels I reviewed since last month, it's still a good entry but not something as magnificently appealing like <i>SAGA</i> or <i>Sex Criminals</i> had proven to be, whose first volumes were immediately so stellar and engrossing. <br><br>I could even liken <i>Y: The Last Man</i> to Joe Hill's debut volume for <i>Locke and Key</i> which had all the proper elements of supernatural horror and drama and has definitely more potentials to sprout from. However, <i>Y: The Last Man</i> in its first volume <i>Unmanned</i> is off to a slow start with the build-up quite scattered among many placed and with different characters that hopefully will form a more cohesive ensemble once the plot progression settles in a more desirable and suspenseful pace. Hey, at least it wasn't <i>The Wicked and Divine</i>, a series I had so much hopes for but sorely let down in the end that I won't even bother posting a review about it. I also didn't bother picking up the second volume anymore because UGH.<br><br>But I digress. Illustrated by Pia Guerra and Jose Marzan Jr., penciler and inker respectively, Y the Las Man was visually efficient enough to convey the dystopic landscape of a man-less existence where women are clamoring for survival, power and politics. The tone of the narrative definitely portrays a satirical approach which calls into question and discussion the topics of female empowerment and the radical extremists who pursue a more vicious goal to assert it. Since all the male mammals including humans got wiped out, these feminazis are inclined to believe that nature has taken its course and now it's time to go Amazonian in such a ridiculously chauvinistic way that DC's counterpart of the real Amazons where Wonder Woman hails from would be ashamed to be associated with these women.<br><br>I can't help but be reminded of that last season of <i>Veronica Mars</i> about said feminazis becoming the villains of that supposedly empowering show. No wonder it got pulled after that season because it was extremely negative in its portrayal of feminist activists. Y: The Last Man, I feel, has a real possibility of crossing that line, but seeing as this was only the first volume and that it did last for ten more, I think I'll assume that the writer and editors of Vertigo found a balance and compromise in how they handled the feminist side of thing for this story. Here are some of the notable pages about it:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474043067i/20547194._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474043067i/20547195._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ongoing discourse about how feminists values and other pro-women movements have been portrayed for Y: The Last Man certainly invites critical arguments from everyone who has their own opinions about it, whether affirmative or cynical. I'd rather stay away from that and simply review and appreciate this as a work of fiction, no matter how politically heated it tends to become in the later issues. Protagonist Yorick and his monkey companion Amerstad are the only male left in the world (or at least as far as we know). Yorick's mother is a congresswoman who wanted him to take his role as mankind's last chance for procreation more seriously, but Yorick is more concerned to getting back to his girlfriend he had just proposed to over a long-distance phone call to Australia before all this extinction shit went down. It's contextually hilarious but also grim.<br><br>As far as first impressions go, I am lukewarm towards Yorick. I don't find him that interesting but he is the central character in an interesting situation. I certainly hope to get to know the other female characters who show a more promising depth but whose names I can't tell you on the spot because of how little time this volume spends presenting them and how thinly the entire storyline is spread across the five issues so far. I do hope I warm up to Yorick especially even if he's such a narrow-minded fool who is more concerned about seeing his girlfriend than discover why the hell has he survived the extinction? I'd be more excited to find that out if I was Yorick, but hey, that's only because I would rather solve a good mystery over any kind of romantic ties I may have.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474043067i/20547196._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Get the fuck out of here, you hopeless sap!</i><br><br>In a nutshell, <i>Y: The Last Man</i> shows promise. It has a puzzle that readers can solve and watch develop across its ten-volumed span, and the feminist angle is certainly worth the merit mentioning as well, but it's not the first graphic novel I will be picking up anytime soon once I finished my scheduled GNs for this year. That place still belongs to <i>SAGA</i>, I'm afraid.<br><br><b>RECOMMENDED: 7/10<br><br>READ MY REVIEWS AT:<br><a href="http://reademption-lit.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416741261i/12051318.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4777323175084704343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1582755877315034496">This book is exactly what the title promises: A plague of some sort kills every mammal on earth with a Y chromosome, except, with no obvious reason for the exception, Yorick Brown and his capuchin monkey, Ampersand. <br/><br/>Chaos ensues as women (and transmen) have to take over running the world. This isn't presented as sexist oh-see-women-can't-handle-it, but as a warning parable about the unhealthy imbalance when entire fields are dominated by one gender. <br/><br/>It's a bit more violent than I would like, but</span>
  <span id="freeText1582755877315034496" style="display:none">This book is exactly what the title promises: A plague of some sort kills every mammal on earth with a Y chromosome, except, with no obvious reason for the exception, Yorick Brown and his capuchin monkey, Ampersand. <br /><br />Chaos ensues as women (and transmen) have to take over running the world. This isn't presented as sexist oh-see-women-can't-handle-it, but as a warning parable about the unhealthy imbalance when entire fields are dominated by one gender. <br /><br />It's a bit more violent than I would like, but it's Vertigo, so I knew what I was getting into. I don't entirely agree with the reactions and directions of the women in the book, but it's someone else's story, and I'm curious to see where he'll take it. <br /><br />My biggest quibble with the story is that no way would Yorick have been given a monkey to train for disabled people when he has (a) no experience training animals, and (b) also no clue about what the eventual recipient of Ampersand might need. Also, weeks after the economy has fallen apart and production and trade of goods has come to a virtual halt, everyone in this book has great hair. <br /><br />I'll definitely be continuing on for at least a few more volumes. </span>

<div id="review_21501238" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21501238" />
    <a title="Jamie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/404400-jamie"><img alt="Jamie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520026973p2/404400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21501238?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie" href="/user/show/404400-jamie">Jamie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21501238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3865540793214768788">Now that I've finished the series (well, the first 9 books -- the 10th is unavailable to me), I'll write a bit about how I feel about the series as a whole.<br/><br/>I really wanted to hate this series. It is incredibly sexist in so many ways, and I started taking notes on some of the more ridiculous aspects of it so I would remember by the time I got around to writing this. My husband would find random pieces of paper scattered around the house and ask me what "factories stop working, no electricity, int</span>
  <span id="freeText3865540793214768788" style="display:none">Now that I've finished the series (well, the first 9 books -- the 10th is unavailable to me), I'll write a bit about how I feel about the series as a whole.<br /><br />I really wanted to hate this series. It is incredibly sexist in so many ways, and I started taking notes on some of the more ridiculous aspects of it so I would remember by the time I got around to writing this. My husband would find random pieces of paper scattered around the house and ask me what "factories stop working, no electricity, internet cafe becomes telegraph center" meant, and I would answer, "Because all the men died, of course!" and we'd laugh about it. The best/worst part is in the 9th book when a comic book reverses the gender wipeout. Instead of all the men, all the women die. All of a sudden, 98% of the secretaries and kindergarten teachers have died! Who knew it would be so devastating? Stupid stuff like this can be a bit infuriating. <br /><br />That said, this series is an enjoyable read if you take it for what it is: a no brainer, page-turning, action packed experience. It's fun, it's quick, it's a good diversion from serious shit. I read each book in one sitting, sometimes two in a day.<br /><br />Most of the female characters in this series look like Maxim models, and even the straight ones engage in hot lesbian sex. It's got every female stereotype you can possibly imagine. On the other hand, the one male left in the world is kind of wimpy. He suffers some ego-shrinking humiliation and overcomes lots of mental insecurities, and he's a decent fellow, an okay guy to be the last guy in the world. I imagine the author of this series to be like him, and this series is his personal fantasy world.<br /><br />I read each book the minute I got my hands on it, but in the end I was really disappointed! What kept me reading was wanting to find out the big mystery of why what happened happened. I already had a good idea of who was responsible, but the why was a huge letdown. Of all the possible reasons... seriously? Lame.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3865540793214768788" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/210747131" />
    <a title="Brandon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3214163-brandon"><img alt="Brandon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603283104p2/3214163.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=after-the-end">after-the-end</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer210747131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12378644507991106485">All the men are <b>dead</b>.<br/><br/>Yorick Brown remains after a mysterious virus eliminates every last thing with a Y chromosome. While he’s expected to do his part in figuring out why he survived, he’s mainly concerned with finding his would-be fiancé in the outback of Australia.<br/><br/>This would be my first experience in reading a graphic novel where the main character isn’t flying/swinging/driving around in spandex. For my first foray into the non-superhero genre, I probably couldn’t have chosen a better series. </span>
  <span id="freeText12378644507991106485" style="display:none">All the men are <b>dead</b>.<br /><br />Yorick Brown remains after a mysterious virus eliminates every last thing with a Y chromosome. While he’s expected to do his part in figuring out why he survived, he’s mainly concerned with finding his would-be fiancé in the outback of Australia.<br /><br />This would be my first experience in reading a graphic novel where the main character isn’t flying/swinging/driving around in spandex. For my first foray into the non-superhero genre, I probably couldn’t have chosen a better series. Not only does it hold a pretty solid spot on most top graphic novel lists, it comes highly recommended by a lot of trusted friends. <br /><br />It’s interesting to see exactly what would happen if the world were suddenly devoid of men. I mean, we <b>are</b> pretty important, right ladies? I kid, I kid. I was actually shocked with how quickly the world was turned upside down. I almost thought that the author was basically saying that women wouldn’t even know what to do, then quickly remembered the sheer amount of work it would take in just disposing of the roughly 2.8 billion bodies.<br /><br />There's lots going on in this opener but it never feels cluttered. We’re following Yorick, we're following the slowly re-established US government, we're following a cult of extremist females named <i>The Amazons</i> and the leader of an Israeli militant group. There's enough here to keep you interested. When I tossed down the first book, I immediately wanted to pick up the next. I can’t wait to get my hands on it.</span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13327769-y">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477266-sarah?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7477266-sarah?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>,

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15806266078107787296">Ok, I thought this would be a comic that portrayed women in a positive way but I was wrong. It's the complete opposite. The women are OH SO HELPLESS without the men. They have no electricity, little food and no proper security. Um why not? If all the men died tomorrow, us women would definitely be able to manage better than the women in this comic. It seems totally illogical to me but I'm willing to give it another chance so it can prove me wrong. I don't understand why the Amazons even exist bu</span>
  <span id="freeText15806266078107787296" style="display:none">Ok, I thought this would be a comic that portrayed women in a positive way but I was wrong. It's the complete opposite. The women are OH SO HELPLESS without the men. They have no electricity, little food and no proper security. Um why not? If all the men died tomorrow, us women would definitely be able to manage better than the women in this comic. It seems totally illogical to me but I'm willing to give it another chance so it can prove me wrong. I don't understand why the Amazons even exist but I'm hoping that I'll figure it out in the next few volumes. I also don't understand why that woman was picking up dead bodies in a crop top and why Beth was hiking in a bikini top, I suppose it's because most females in comic books are overly-sexualised. I don't like the main character, he is a bit of an ass but he might grow on me yet! I really liked the artwork. I'll keep reading to see if this picks up because I feel like it has potential.</span>

Yorick is a bit daft, but I have a feeling there's room for growth here. <br/><br/>It's the end of the world and somehow all the males are dead (except for Yorick and his male "assistant" shoulder monkey), and instead of a zombie apocalypse it's a bunch of raging female extremists who are the enemy. There's some political jokes aimed at everyone and a few pop culture references to appreciate. <br /><br />I am definitely interested in continuing the series. I don't think it is as mind-blowing as some of the cover blurb quotes said... but there is good potential here.<br /><br /></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>,
